  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_dd741536-9005-4f5d-b1bd-a3a18e9a9d59'
      });
    }
    
    var initializeSiwa = function() {
      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"
      loadScript(APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL, initAppleId);
    };

      initAppleId();

      initializeSiwa();

  <span id="freeText4719835513958953031" style="display:none">إن رواية الساعة الخامسة والعشرون أحد أكثر الأعمال السردية الباعثة على أسئلة جذرية حول مصير الإنسان المأسوي ، فعالم الرواية الافتراضي متاهة يتعذر أن ينجو منها أحد . وعلى النقيض من معظم الأعمال السردية حيث يختل توازن الأحداث ثم يعاد في النهاية ، فإن نسق الاختلال يتعمق بمرور الزمن ، ولا يعود إلى سابق عهده أبداً <br />رواية تتجلى فيها أصداء الملاحم الكبرى ، والتراجيديات الإغريقية و المآسي الشكسبيرية ، ومجمل الأعمال التي انصب اهتمامها عل مصير الإنسان ، لذلك فهي تنتسب إلى سلالة الآداب السردية الرفيعة الخالدة <br />كثير من الروايات يتلاشى حضوره مع الذاكرة بمرور الأيام ، وتصبح استعادة أجوائه صعبة ، وربما شبه مستحيلة ،وقليل منها يدمغ الذاكرة بختمه الأبدي ، ومن ذلك القليل النادر رواية الساعة الخامسة والعشرون.</span>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Giovani Salvador" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Giovani Salvador" href="/user/show/11536550-giovani-salvador">Giovani Salvador</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1559286407" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3981076852312833989">There are 2 things in this book that astonished me:<br/>The first, is the level of details on the horrors of the war. Since the author lived the war cruelty, he was able to describe things that other books or movies could not capture accurately. One of the biggest things was the author's own experience: Innocent man, being thrown from concentration camp to concentration camp. Living the horrors of the bureaucracy, where one's own desire or story is not taken into account. Where forms are more trustwo</span>
  <span id="freeText3981076852312833989" style="display:none">There are 2 things in this book that astonished me:<br />The first, is the level of details on the horrors of the war. Since the author lived the war cruelty, he was able to describe things that other books or movies could not capture accurately. One of the biggest things was the author's own experience: Innocent man, being thrown from concentration camp to concentration camp. Living the horrors of the bureaucracy, where one's own desire or story is not taken into account. Where forms are more trustworthy than facts. Where you are first guilty and later, maybe, innocent.<br /> <br />The second thing, more related to the society as a whole, is how him (Virgil) was able to visualize the transformation of the man into <br />a machine built to serve bigger interests. Corporations, government, etc, the big interest had always been in mass control, in seeing mankind collectively. From one regime to another, from left to right wing, what matters is mass control. To keep people busy, not having time to think.<br /><br />I finished reading this book almost crying with his (real) story. </span>
  <a data-text-id="3981076852312833989" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2047196352" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2047196352" />
    <a title="Bert van der Vaart" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/58591610-bert-van-der-vaart"><img alt="Bert van der Vaart" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/u_50x66-632230dc9882b4352d753eedf9396530.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2047196352?book_show_action=true">Jul 02, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Bert van der Vaart" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Bert van der Vaart" href="/user/show/58591610-bert-van-der-vaart">Bert van der Vaart</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback " href="/book/show/17621210-het-25e-uur">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2047196352" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2045088584444102064">Originally written in French by a Romanian writer, I found a Dutch translation in a second hand book store in a small town in northeast NL, which was an edition published before ISBN numbers were made. The book is a superb exposition of the danger of governments treating people generically, as classes or groups of undifferentiated beings--and then having bureaucrats manage these groups as homogenous masses. Set in 1935-1948, it goes through the confusion of WW II and the conflicting governments </span>
  <span id="freeText2045088584444102064" style="display:none">Originally written in French by a Romanian writer, I found a Dutch translation in a second hand book store in a small town in northeast NL, which was an edition published before ISBN numbers were made. The book is a superb exposition of the danger of governments treating people generically, as classes or groups of undifferentiated beings--and then having bureaucrats manage these groups as homogenous masses. Set in 1935-1948, it goes through the confusion of WW II and the conflicting governments by Nazis, Communists, and the soi disant enlightened western military powers. The thesis is that, because of technological advances, government authorities tend to look at people as input factors ("citizens"), which organizationally perhaps (though unlikely) allows government to help sort out its "citizens"' basic economic survival. However, in doing so, these governments/organizations completely ignore and fail to deal with the individual and spiritual characteristics of the "person". Citizens may at some stage have been in control but will wind up "serving" the machinery of government and in the end becoming impersonal and unfulfilled "techno-slaves". Provocative and very worthwhile read, if you can find a copy!</span>
  <a data-text-id="2045088584444102064" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>


      <div class="reviewFooter uitext buttons">

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8289380?shelf=favoriten">favoriten</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1033563186" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13851775664989894981">An unputdownable book, it was so overwhelming that I didn't want to finish it, but, at the same time, I wanted so badly to finish it just to end the pain of Johann Moritz, Sisyphus of his time!</span>

          </span>

<div id="review_3349475762" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3349475762" />
    <a title="Tbfrank" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/901924-tbfrank"><img alt="Tbfrank" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/u_50x66-632230dc9882b4352d753eedf9396530.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3349475762?book_show_action=true">Jun 07, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Tbfrank" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Tbfrank" href="/user/show/901924-tbfrank">Tbfrank</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover " href="/book/show/6560520-twenty-fifth-hour">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3349475762" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5029710983777074827">The author adopts the technique of establishing a character as a novelist writing a book with the same title. This character intends to follow the lives of perhaps 10 persons in his home village as they approach the 25th hour, the hour after human civilization has ceased to exist, subordinated to and consumed by a fully mechanized society. Having completed four chapters, he becomes a victim of the remorseless advance of the impersonal society where human beings count for nothing and truth become</span>
  <span id="freeText5029710983777074827" style="display:none">The author adopts the technique of establishing a character as a novelist writing a book with the same title. This character intends to follow the lives of perhaps 10 persons in his home village as they approach the 25th hour, the hour after human civilization has ceased to exist, subordinated to and consumed by a fully mechanized society. Having completed four chapters, he becomes a victim of the remorseless advance of the impersonal society where human beings count for nothing and truth becomes what is written on a piece of paper - and what the men with the guns decide it is.<br /><br />The primary impressions the reader may take away from this book:<br />1) The birth and condemnation of Technical Civilization which devalues the individual by defining them as interchangeable parts; <br />2) How the peasants vacillate between unwarranted hope and acceptance of their brutal fate imposed by one power group after another;<br />3) Some of what post-WW2 life in Europe was like, the exchange of one set of camps and jailers for another;<br />4) The distinction of the Cold War (which reached hot status) as an internal revolution of the Technical Civilization, the East (USSR) having absorbed the Western ideas, adding only a peculiar brutal facet to the mix.<br /><br />A sad and haunting story which rings chillingly true - then and now.<br />One might imagine this as a prelude to Orwell's 1984.</span>
  <a data-text-id="5029710983777074827" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('1hNVazCY+mWRQiRma5Kh9Rwv1jw8TlMzqroUaSaqhWbD/Xy5qIqTETW8enLqtZS//7xWtGCuInc7s+yJW1L/UQ==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('Te3lV0i01JrLyfkkuOtiBkYuEfKzTdrEYA+31JXtoa9YA8yF0Ka97m83pzA5zFdMpb2Reu+tq4DxBk806BXbmA==')})
  }

هدر الكثير من الجهد والوقت والإمكانات المادية، بشكل اتخذ طابع التبذير الذي لا يمكن للمجتمع المتخلف، ذي الأعباء الثقال، أن يسمح لنفسه به. انطلق هؤلاء جميعا في مشاريع تنموية طنانة، ذات بريق ووجاهة، قائمة على دراسات ومخططات جزئية، لم تتجاوز السطح معظم الأحيان، كي تنفذ إلى دينامية البنية المتخلفة من ناحية ، أو إلى التكوين النفسي والذهني للإنسان المتخلف الذي أريد تطويره من ناحية ثانية. وضعت خطط مستوردة عن نماذج طبقت ونجحت في بلدان صناعية، ولكن مسيرة هذه الخطط لم تخط بعيدة، فلقد أخففت التجارب المستوردة، والمشاريع الملصقة من الخارج، كما فشلت المشاريع ذات الطابع الدعائي الاستعراضي في تحريك بنية المجتمع ككل، وفي الارتقاء بإنسان ذلك المجتمع.\nذلك لأن إنسان هذه المجتمعات لم ينظر إليه باعتباره عنصرة أساسية ومحورية في أي خطة تنموية . التنمية، مهما كان میدانها، ثمن تغير الإنسان ونظرته إلى الأمور في المقام الأول. لا بد إذا من وضع الأمور في إطارها البشري الصحيح، وأخذ خصائص الفئة السكانية التي يراد تطوير نمط حياتها بعين الاعتبار. ولا بد بالتالي من دراسة هذه الخصائص ومعرفة بنيتها ودينامينها، وهو ما ترومه هذه المحاولة، بما قد تحمل من ثغرات، تطمح إلى فتح الطريق أمام أبحاث نفسية ميدانية ، تحاول فهم الإنسان المتخلف بنوعيته وخصوصية وضعه، وبشكل حي وواقعي، لتكون مرتكزات علم نفس التخلف.<\/span>\n  <a
